    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer817436544179067798">When a passenger check-in desk at London's Heathrow Airport disappears in a ball of orange flame, the explosion is deemed an act of God. And what has this to do with Dirk's latest--and late-- client, found only this morning with his head revolv</span>
  <span id="freeText817436544179067798" style="display:none">When a passenger check-in desk at London's Heathrow Airport disappears in a ball of orange flame, the explosion is deemed an act of God. But which god, wonders holistic detective Dirk Gently? What god would be hanging around Heathrow trying to catch the 3:37 to Oslo? And what has this to do with Dirk's latest--and late-- client, found only this morning with his head revolving atop the hit record "Hot Potato"? Amid the hostile attentions of a stray eagle and the trauma of a very dirty refrigerator, super-sleuth Dirk Gently will once again solve the mysteries of the universe...</span>
  <a data-text-id="817436544179067798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/15840956-rick-patterson"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1356672864i/15840956._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/15840956-rick-patterson">Rick Patterson</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The very last lines of the book indicate that Dirk is going to read the news and discover that his flat has been utterly destroyed by the former eagle<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The very last lines of the book indicate that Dirk is going to read the news and discover that his flat has been utterly destroyed by the former eagle (now restored [just for a second or two] as a fighter jet). The lawyer and advertising agent couple have been disposed of by the timely re-appearance of this jet, so their contract with Odin is dispensed with anyway, even without Thor's legal appeal, which is clearly successful because he gets back his powers in order to transform the eagle back to the fighter jet. Are you following all of this? Adams seems to finish the book a bit abruptly, yes, but these elements are all there to be picked up. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_570498027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570498027" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570498027?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2017-shelf">2017-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570498027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1201604549447743498">I had to re-read this because I'm insane but I'm happy to be so because I still loved it.<br/><br/>Total truth time: it's not quite as funny or as sharp in the individual zinger lines as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/365.Dirk_Gently_s_Holistic_Detective_Agency__Dirk_Gently__1_' title='Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency (Dirk Gently #1) by Douglas Adams' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency</a>, but the long-running story gags are fantastically wicked and cruel and even profoundly sad.<br/><br/>It's also more of an adventure tale for Dirk later on, but primarily, it's all a mystery. Sometimes, the plot is as much of a mystery, too, but I don't care. :) After the rising of new gods i</span>
  <span id="freeText1201604549447743498" style="display:none">I had to re-read this because I'm insane but I'm happy to be so because I still loved it.<br /><br />Total truth time: it's not quite as funny or as sharp in the individual zinger lines as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/365.Dirk_Gently_s_Holistic_Detective_Agency__Dirk_Gently__1_" title="Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency (Dirk Gently #1) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency</a>, but the long-running story gags are fantastically wicked and cruel and even profoundly sad.<br /><br />It's also more of an adventure tale for Dirk later on, but primarily, it's all a mystery. Sometimes, the plot is as much of a mystery, too, but I don't care. :) After the rising of new gods in Asgard and the fate of soooo many pebbles, and the dark, dark fate of a Coke machine, who really cares? The novel is brilliant and creative and so darkly funny. It's enough to make me despair for modern literature, and this came out in '88! <br /><br />Here's another awesome tidbit. It's the novel that I first thought of when I first read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30165203.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_" title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a>. All the greatness of seeing Odin on the page or Thor blowing up an airport is all here and the characterizations are brilliant. <br /><br />Can I even say that it's even more brilliant after knowing the legends much better? You bet I can! I read this when I was 14 years old the first time and let's be frank... I didn't know crap. I learned most of what I knew about Thor from this book and the fact that there was some silly Marvel comic that I wasn't even tempted to read was about it. And now? Soooooo Nice! :) Even the little In-Jokes about the gods are all here. It's a bit more erudite than I expected it to be. :)<br /><br />But it's also so funny! Do I love eagles even more now? You bet! Am I even more annoyed with Yuppies? You bet! Do I want to run out and get some 300 count sheets and snuggle in them, perhaps get an eyepatch and avoid big strapping men with hammers? You bet!<br /><br />Poor Dirk. I have to admit that his Horoscope is always dead-on. :)<br /><br />My one complaint is that there wasn't a whole series made out of this. I still wonder just how amazingly cool it could have been to have a full bookcase full of these and point to it as the most amazing thing EVAH.<br /><br />*sigh*<br /><br />Some authors just overflow with goodness. Douglas Adams was one of them. *sigh*</span>
  <a data-text-id="1201604549447743498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1942361341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942361341" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942361341?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447221104" href="/book/show/17057265-the-long-dark-tea-time-of-the-soul">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942361341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8405161015018587674">This is the second book about Dirk Gently, the holistic private investigator. A seriously underestimated series (or what was to become a series, I'm sure).<br/> <br/>In this second volume, Dirk is not really at his best. Something is wrong and he can't put his finger to it. To make matters worse, a very well off client, who promised to voluntarily pay for all sorts of quirks, is not just crazy as Dirk had thought, but ends up dead (money sure does seem to have a way of getting away from Dirk). Dirk's horo</span>
  <span id="freeText8405161015018587674" style="display:none">This is the second book about Dirk Gently, the holistic private investigator. A seriously underestimated series (or what was to become a series, I'm sure).<br /> <br />In this second volume, Dirk is not really at his best. Something is wrong and he can't put his finger to it. To make matters worse, a very well off client, who promised to voluntarily pay for all sorts of quirks, is not just crazy as Dirk had thought, but ends up dead (money sure does seem to have a way of getting away from Dirk). Dirk's horoscope is even worse than usual but instead of taking the holistic approach, he chalks it up to an acquaintance of his being even more annoying than usual (that acquaintance is writing that particular horoscope). Add to that a weird incident at Heathrow airport (it had it coming if you ask me, I hate that place) and several encounters with fridges and a Coca-Cola vending machine and you get the usual silliness for which Douglas Adams was so famous for.<br /><br />However, as is also signature DA, no matter how silly his characters or observations, they are also spot on. Like how airports are the worst places on Earth and how everyone is aggravated there. Or how the simplest things we're used to can seem paramount when living somewhere this simple thing isn't normal and certainly not simple (yes, I'm talking about the pizza deliveries - Paul, is it true that London doesn't have (or didn't have, in the 80s?) pizza delivering services, but that you have (had?) to pick the pizza up yourself instead?).<br /> <br />Throughout the book there are hilarious moments, classics of the comedy genre. Like when Kate is at Heathrow in the very beginning. Or when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the eagle is in Dirk's office/apartment, he locks it in the kitchen, it repeatedly flies against the kitchen door in order to get out, then Dirk opens the door, the eagle doesn't notice in time and instead slams into the wall of the next room <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Or how Kate often gets revenge for not having a pizza delivery service in London. In fact, her interaction with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Thor <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in general. Or how Dirk gets his Jaguar from the mechanic (see below). Or how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a certain couple got what they had coming <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> at the very end of the book. <br />I was once again involuntarily attracting a lot of attention on my commute home when I burst out laughing on several occasions.<br /> <br />Here, for those who already know the book or want to laugh but not read the book (*gasps* shame on you all!):<br /><br /><i>He did at last understand that the mechanic was also claiming that a family of starlings had at some point in the past made their nest in a sensitive part of the engine's workings and had subsequently perished horribly, taking sensitive parts of the engine with them, and at this point Dirk began to cast about himself desperately for what to do.<br />He noticed that the mechanic's pick-up truck was standing nearby with its engine still running, and elected to make off with this instead. Being a slightly less slow and cumbersome runner than the mechanic he was able to put this plan into operation with a minimum of difficulty.<br />He swung out into the lane, drove off into the night and parked three miles down the road. He left the van's lights on, let down its tyres, and hid himself behind a tree. After about ten minutes his Jaguar came hurtling round the corner, passed the van, hauled itself to an abrupt halt and reversed wildly back towards it. The mechanic threw open the door, leapt out and hurried over to reclaim his property, leaving Dirk with the opportunity he needed to leap from behind the tree and reclaim his own. <br />He spun his wheels pointedly and drove off in a kind of grim triumph, ...</i><br /><br />Or this little gem:<br /><i>An "Act of God". Merely a chance, careless phrase by which people were able to dispose conveniently of awkward phenomena that would admit of no more rational explanation. But it was the chance carelessness of it which particularly appealed to Dirk because words used carelessly, as if they did not matter in any serious way, often allowed otherwise well-guarded truths to seep through.</i><br /> <br />One thing was scary: the lawyer? The whole time I read the speech he gave Dirk I kept hearing Donald Trump (you know, the pronunciation, the repetition, "the greatest", ...)!<br /><br />Nevertheless, despite such golden moments of comedy and the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Norse gods (my second favourite canon) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were in this, I didn't love this as much as the first book. Maybe it was because Dirk wasn't on top of his game and I kept screaming at him internally that he had already noticed the significant bits, just subconsciously. Or because although there were sharp observations in this as well, they weren't as sharp or as numerous as in the first book. I don't know. However, those are also very strong emotions the book invoked and the writing style was once again top notch and very engaging, the characters all quirky and realistic though (or especially because) extremely whacky.<br /> <br />Before writing this review, I intended to "only" give this 4 stars to mark the difference between this and the previous volume. However, now that I've gathered my thoughts for this review, I think that would be an injustice - the first one was perfection from start to finish, this one was "only" but still excellent after all. Thus, I'm giving it 5 stars yet again, because I'm a solid Douglas Adams fangirl now and it is clear that I love Dirk Gently and am thoroughly saddened by how soon the series has had to come to an end. <br />I'll definitely finish this up by also reading the "3rd" (actually just a collection of what Douglas Adams had prepared for a third novel plus some other bits and pieces he might have turned into books had he not died much too soon).</span>
  <a data-text-id="8405161015018587674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2813479598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2813479598" />
    <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton"><img alt="J.L.   Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438142892p2/3675162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2813479598?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.L.   Sutton" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton">J.L.   Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32719922-the-long-dark-tea-time-of-the-soul">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2813479598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer435820843360695385">So the title The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul is so fantastic! And the randomness, quirkiness and interesting meditations of Douglas Adams's detective, Dirk Gently, matches the tone set by that title. The novel even features the Norse Gods in the modern world (reminding me of Neil Gaiman's American Gods). Definitely a different take on Thor than you'll see in the superhero movies. The mystery/plot(s) are less the point here than simply taking the journey. In that respect, there's a commonality</span>
  <span id="freeText435820843360695385" style="display:none">So the title The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul is so fantastic! And the randomness, quirkiness and interesting meditations of Douglas Adams's detective, Dirk Gently, matches the tone set by that title. The novel even features the Norse Gods in the modern world (reminding me of Neil Gaiman's American Gods). Definitely a different take on Thor than you'll see in the superhero movies. The mystery/plot(s) are less the point here than simply taking the journey. In that respect, there's a commonality with Adams' more famous Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy series. Getting to the restaurant at the end of the universe, for instance, is more important than the destination. For me, the randomness can be too random at times and not at all connected to plot, but again, I know that wasn't the point. I enjoyed! 3.75 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="435820843360695385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115090193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11134087243423325680">Almost entirely, but not quite, unlike tea–I mean, The Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy. There is no way easy way to say this, but despite ingredients that should be interesting, it just fails to work for me. However, unlike American Gods, which resembles it more than a bit, it is entirely more palatable and has 100% less offensive scenes, so there is that (I may have some trouble with statistics here). Nonetheless, because it is contains some Douglas Adamsisms that have stuck with me through th</span>
  <span id="freeText11134087243423325680" style="display:none">Almost entirely, but not quite, unlike tea–I mean, The Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy. There is no way easy way to say this, but despite ingredients that should be interesting, it just fails to work for me. However, unlike American Gods, which resembles it more than a bit, it is entirely more palatable and has 100% less offensive scenes, so there is that (I may have some trouble with statistics here). Nonetheless, because it is contains some Douglas Adamsisms that have stuck with me through the years, it still had moments of brilliance. Take his airport rule, for instance:<br /><b><br />“It can hardly be a coincidence that no language on earth has ever produced the expression ‘As pretty as an airport.’<br />Airports are ugly. Some are very ugly. Some attain a degree of ugliness that can only be the result of a special effort. This ugliness arises because airports are full of people who are tired, cross, and have just discovered that their luggage has landed in Murmansk (Murmansk airport is the only known exception to this otherwise infallible rule), and architects have on the whole tried to reflect this in their designs.”<br /></b><br />This is true. There is nothing about any airport that is pretty. Most people there are indeed tired and cross, which is why when they discover that their plane has been delayed, or cancelled, or erupted in flames, they tend to overreact.<br /><br /><br /><br />But an airport is just the beginning of roughly three separate plot lines, give or take; a young woman who is thwarted from a vacation to Oslo by a mysterious giant of a man and a fireball blowing up the check-in counter; Dirk Gently, a detective who is hired to protect an unethical producer; and a mysterious old man who would like to lay in bed and be gently catered to by a team of nursing staff. Dirk’s own adventures further degenerate into conflicts with a large eagle and a malevolent refrigerator. It’s all very puzzling mostly due to the narrative breaks and confused protagonists more than any real mystery on the part of the universe.<br /><br />Having been a fan of Hitchhikers and frequent re-listener to Stephen Fry’s reading, I couldn’t help but see similarities between the lead characters. Dirk comes across like a slightly smarter version of Zaphod and Arthur, a strange mix of lucky and clueless. I don’t know that he ‘solves’ anything so much as stumbles unto the solution. The young woman, Kate, is quite literally, taken for a ride and had some of the general non-descriptiveness feel that I always got from Trillian. <br /><br />Mostly, Tea-Time contains entertaining interludes and observations loosely connected by plot. To me, it works better in wacky unreal space adventures than in a mystery.<br /><br />When I was young, I was an enormous fan of The Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy. I must have read it ten times. I bought whatever I could then lay my teenage hands on, written by Mr. Adams. But the Dirk Gently series never really gelled with me. Was it a window of interest? I sold off the first, but the title of the second was too, too appropriate to let go. For years I have thought of that saying, that mysterious four o’clock ennui of the soul (both am and pm) and thought that the book deserved a re-read on that alone, as well as notes on a driving technique which I’ve totally used (Note it works much better in rural areas and suburbs).<br /><b><br />“Perhaps it would save time if he went back to get his car, but then again it was only a short distance, and he had a tremendous propensity for getting lost when driving. This was largely because of his ‘Zen’ method of navigation, which was simply to find any car that looked as if it knew where it was going and follow it. The results were more often surprising than successful, but he felt it was worth it for the sake of the few occasions when it was both.”</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11134087243423325680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_4120713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4120713" />
    <a title="Thorir2007" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/253182-thorir2007"><img alt="Thorir2007" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1186252953p2/253182.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4120713?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thorir2007" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thorir2007" href="/user/show/253182-thorir2007">Thorir2007</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671694043" href="/book/show/76615.The_Long_Dark_Tea_Time_of_the_Soul">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/253182-thorir2007?shelf=greatbooks">greatbooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4120713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13052659321538586238">Unlike his “Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy” series (a collection of humorous vignettes without much of a plot, continuity, or character development), Douglas Adams’ Dirk Gently series (two novels and some sketches for a third one, included in the “Salmon of Doubt”) is in fact literature of the first degree. In the second novel, “<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/357.The_Long_Dark_Tea_Time_of_the_Soul' title='The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul by Douglas Adams' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul</a>,” Dirk Gently, a private “holistic” investigator (an eccentric slob, perpetually broke, capricious, silly, and wonderfully insightfu</span>
  <span id="freeText13052659321538586238" style="display:none">Unlike his “Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy” series (a collection of humorous vignettes without much of a plot, continuity, or character development), Douglas Adams’ Dirk Gently series (two novels and some sketches for a third one, included in the “Salmon of Doubt”) is in fact literature of the first degree. In the second novel, “<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/357.The_Long_Dark_Tea_Time_of_the_Soul" title="The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul</a>,” Dirk Gently, a private “holistic” investigator (an eccentric slob, perpetually broke, capricious, silly, and wonderfully insightful), while minding his client’s (Kate, a somewhat confused gal from New York) interests, unravels a pseudo-conspiracy involving the Norse gods (all of them), in which the gods are the victims.<br /><br />Employing his own special methods (which differ from Sherlock Holmes’ methods in that Dirk has a soft spot for the impossible and does not like to dismiss it), Dirk manages to a) side with the gods b) save them c) punish the guilty d) help his client e) end up broke again. The last bit is fine by him (in the previous novel, he sent a bill to a client of his, whose missing cat he was supposed to find, with just one item on it, “Saving the Universe. No charge”).<br /><br />Laced with Adams’ trademark humor, this novel certainly puts its author in the same category with Mark Twain, Chekhov, and Maupassant. I’m not exaggerating. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13052659321538586238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_459735646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459735646" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459735646?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459735646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17329912208520538036">This used to be one of my favorite books when I was 18 (that was more than a few years ago *cough* thirty something *cough*). I was definitely going through a ‘I love everything Douglas Adams’ phase at the time and while I still like this book because sometimes the ridiculousness of the plot and randomness of how everything happens is still so much fun I didn’t enjoy it as much as I did back then.<br/><br/>There are some great things in this. There is Dirk who is a funny and severely quirky character who </span>
  <span id="freeText17329912208520538036" style="display:none">This used to be one of my favorite books when I was 18 (that was more than a few years ago *cough* thirty something *cough*). I was definitely going through a ‘I love everything Douglas Adams’ phase at the time and while I still like this book because sometimes the ridiculousness of the plot and randomness of how everything happens is still so much fun I didn’t enjoy it as much as I did back then.<br /><br />There are some great things in this. There is Dirk who is a funny and severely quirky character who is often very creative in his role as a holistic detective. I really do laugh at the odd way in which he sees the world and interacts with it. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“He had a tremendous propensity for getting lost when driving. This was largely because of his method of <b>“Zen” navigation, which was simply to find any car that looked as if it knew where it was going and follow it.</b> The results were more often surprising than successful, but he felt it was worth it for the sake of the few occasions when it was both.” <br /><br />“When the girl sitting at the next table looked away for a moment, <b>Dirk leaned over and took her coffee. He knew that he was perfectly safe doing this because she would simply not be able to believe that this had happened</b>. He sat sipping at the lukewarm cup and casting his mind back over the day.” </i>
</blockquote><br />While if I met him in real life I’d probably like to deck him, in the story I find his antics and musings completely fascinating and sometimes hilarious.<br /><br />Some of the story seemed more like just random events to me this time through and while situationally funny I wasn’t sure how it all moved together sometimes. <b>Thor having performance issues was entertaining</b> as was Kate trying to figure out why right after she left the ticketing gate at Heathrow Airport did it blow un and what is with all the penguins in her subconscious.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Insofar as she recognized at all that she was dreaming, she realized that she must be exploring her subconscious mind. She had heard it said that humans are supposed only to use about a tenth of their brains, and that no one was really clear what the other nine tenths were for, but she had certainly never heard it suggested that they were used for storing penguins.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Adams wrote some wonderful jokes throughout the story</b> but now that I’ve read so many more books I see where there are some real pacing problems and the actual story is a bit lackluster overall, but the jokes are great.<br /><br /><b>Even though this isn’t as great as I once remembered it being I still so love to dive into this type of humor from time to time and just give into the improbability and impossibility of it all</b>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17329912208520538036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168822216" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168822216" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168822216?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780330309554" href="/book/show/823660.The_Long_Dark_Tea_time_of_the_Soul">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=whodunnit">whodunnit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168822216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14367042214027592920">20,000 ratings, 500 reviews? Why bother to add another one to the masses? You don't need me to tell you to read this book, if you've gotten this far you're either already a fan of Adams or like me you picked it up because of the moody title and should have now found out that it's a sequel to the original <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/365.Dirk_Gently_s_Holistic_Detective_Agency__Dirk_Gently___1_' title='Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency (Dirk Gently, #1) by Douglas Adams' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency</a>. Fear not, you don't really need to have read the other one to enjoy this additional piece of absurdity from Douglas Adams. Instead I'll make five points </span>
  <span id="freeText14367042214027592920" style="display:none">20,000 ratings, 500 reviews? Why bother to add another one to the masses? You don't need me to tell you to read this book, if you've gotten this far you're either already a fan of Adams or like me you picked it up because of the moody title and should have now found out that it's a sequel to the original <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/365.Dirk_Gently_s_Holistic_Detective_Agency__Dirk_Gently___1_" title="Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency (Dirk Gently, #1) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency</a>. Fear not, you don't really need to have read the other one to enjoy this additional piece of absurdity from Douglas Adams. Instead I'll make five points about the second Dirk Gently if I may.<br /><br />1. I've read this book more than any other Douglas Adams book.<br /><br />2. This is my good friend Emily's favourite ever book; she loves it so much that she judges people by whether they have it on their bookshelf or not, whether they've even read it and most importantly how much they enjoyed it. Happily I still enjoyed this book, my friendship with Emily is safe.<br /><br />3. The BBC TV series recently aired and was totally and completely brilliant, the performance of Stephen Mangan as Dirk Gently is as close to perfection as you get in a TV adaptation. So good was his performance that I read through this book today and could only imagine him as Dirk, as if Adams wrote it with him in mind (impossible but Dirk doesn't have any problems with impossible, as long as he can find out how it's done.)<br /><br />4. Written in 1987 apparently pizza was not delivered in the UK at this time. The horror! I cannot imagine a world where you can't get pizza delivered. No wonder Pizza Hut was such a big thing when it opened in my town as a child.<br /><br />5. Combining the content of this novel and the fact that he wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/79257.Don_t_Panic_The_Official_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy_Companion" title="Don't Panic The Official Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy Companion by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Don't Panic: The Official Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy Companion</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a> was clearly influenced by Adams when writing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods" title="American Gods by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a> AND for the first time I realised that some of the parts of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12067.Good_Omens" title="Good Omens by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Omens</a> I'd attributed to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a> in my mind were obviously examples of early Gaiman.<br /><br />And there you have it, another collection of words written about this book on GR. Well worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14367042214027592920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2573141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2573141" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/160267-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1183076143p2/160267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2573141?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/160267-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780330309554" href="/book/show/823660.The_Long_Dark_Tea_time_of_the_Soul">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Douglas Adams fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2573141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer515496260576156494">Unfortunately, Adams' sequel to <b>Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency</b> isn't as tightly-written as its predecessor. On the sentence level, Adams is still writing furiously funny jokes, but <b>The Long, Dark Tea-Time of the Soul</b> ends up feeling like first-class humor wrapped loosely around second-class plot and characters. Adams has been accused of writing punchlines rather than plots, and it shows in this book perhaps more so than anywhere else. I also thought the book's flow suffered greatly in p</span>
  <span id="freeText515496260576156494" style="display:none">Unfortunately, Adams' sequel to <b>Dirk Gently's Holistic Detective Agency</b> isn't as tightly-written as its predecessor. On the sentence level, Adams is still writing furiously funny jokes, but <b>The Long, Dark Tea-Time of the Soul</b> ends up feeling like first-class humor wrapped loosely around second-class plot and characters. Adams has been accused of writing punchlines rather than plots, and it shows in this book perhaps more so than anywhere else. I also thought the book's flow suffered greatly in places, with important scenes not having enough space devoted to their development (especially in the last few pages, such as the Valhalla scene). In addition, Dirk Gently's "fundamental interconnectedness" approach to investigation--where everything is important because it's linked to everything else--is still present here, but the linked items don't line up as neatly as they did in the first book. I also found the conclusion lacking: at the end of <b>Dirk Gently's...</b>, I said "Fantastic!" aloud to the room around me; at the end of <b>The Long, Dark...</b> I turned the page and, when there was nothing else to read, said aloud, "That's it?" So: five stars for humor, but minus two for poor plot and flow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="515496260576156494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

How often have you been presented with an apparently rational explanation of something that works in all respects other than one, which is just that it is hopelessly improbable? We should therefore be very suspicious of it and all its specious rationality."<br /><br />Words to live by. Stay open-minded, because there's a lot we don't know about.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17168680050796338475">This is very hard for me, you know? I love Douglas Adams; I adore his phrasing, his word structure, and how he manages to make things seem funny,ridiculous, menacing or heartbreaking. I've loved the Hitchhiker books, and he continues to be one of the writers I care for quite immensely.<br/><br/>This is why rating this book as 3/5 is so sad for me, this book started off great, with plenty of intrigue and mystery, and a bunch of characters that seemed interesting and off their rockers (in other words, regul</span>
  <span id="freeText17168680050796338475" style="display:none">This is very hard for me, you know? I love Douglas Adams; I adore his phrasing, his word structure, and how he manages to make things seem funny,ridiculous, menacing or heartbreaking. I've loved the Hitchhiker books, and he continues to be one of the writers I care for quite immensely.<br /><br />This is why rating this book as 3/5 is so sad for me, this book started off great, with plenty of intrigue and mystery, and a bunch of characters that seemed interesting and off their rockers (in other words, regular Adams fare). So, I thought I was going to love it, and I did!<br /><br />But then I came to the last few chapters, and it seems like someone was on Adams's case, asking him to finish the damn book. The whole thing seems hurried, with characters jumping around and events taking place so fast that you couldn't even tell what had happened until you've read it again. His randomness, which is endearing when used carefully, is tossed about everywhere, as he ties up every single loose end in a matter of a few paragraphs.<br /><br />I won't lie; I felt cheated by the end of this book, and I don't like to be cheated.</span>

<div id="review_4446505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4446505" />
    <a title="John Wiswell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/147818-john-wiswell"><img alt="John Wiswell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442531848p2/147818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4446505?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Wiswell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Wiswell" href="/user/show/147818-john-wiswell">John Wiswell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy readers, sci fi readers, theology readers, humor readers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4446505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7822012230433417373">Adams' bizarre book is more of an adventure than a mystery, and more of a picaresque than an adventure. It's true, this plot wanders and is flimsy at times, but Adams always makes up for it with clever insights and hilarious jokes. Minor events mushroom at the end to unexpected relevance, a very bold literary move that would be a sign of laziness if these moves didn't work and we didn't recognize Adams' competence as a writer from the execution of his humor throughout. Fantasy readers and Adams'</span>
  <span id="freeText7822012230433417373" style="display:none">Adams' bizarre book is more of an adventure than a mystery, and more of a picaresque than an adventure. It's true, this plot wanders and is flimsy at times, but Adams always makes up for it with clever insights and hilarious jokes. Minor events mushroom at the end to unexpected relevance, a very bold literary move that would be a sign of laziness if these moves didn't work and we didn't recognize Adams' competence as a writer from the execution of his humor throughout. Fantasy readers and Adams' fans will have an easier time with some of the leaps in logic (such as what happens to a god when nobody believes in it), and most readers shouldn't expect a hardline plot after the first hundred pages of inaction and wild action. You go along with Adams because of his creativity, exhibited in such things as derogatory horoscopes, depressed deities and a philosophical calculater. His writing style is so absurd that, unless you don't hitch onto the entertainment value and profound ramifications, you ought to appreciate the absurd plotting that works as its product.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7822012230433417373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123512719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123512719" />
    <a title="F.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1309606-f-r"><img alt="F.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544886612p2/1309606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123512719?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="F.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="F.R." href="/user/show/1309606-f-r">F.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780330309554" href="/book/show/823660.The_Long_Dark_Tea_time_of_the_Soul">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123512719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13696850037546573302">As much as I enjoyed ‘Dirk Gently’s Holistic Detective Agency’, I have to say that ‘The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul’ is the better book. The reason for that is simple – you get more Dirk for your pound! Whereas it was halfway through before this most intriguing of detectives put in an appearance in the first novel, here he arrives in Chapter Three – waging a war with his cleaner as to which of them is actually going to open the fridge door (something which hasn’t been done in over three month</span>
  <span id="freeText13696850037546573302" style="display:none">As much as I enjoyed ‘Dirk Gently’s Holistic Detective Agency’, I have to say that ‘The Long Dark Tea-Time of the Soul’ is the better book. The reason for that is simple – you get more Dirk for your pound! Whereas it was halfway through before this most intriguing of detectives put in an appearance in the first novel, here he arrives in Chapter Three – waging a war with his cleaner as to which of them is actually going to open the fridge door (something which hasn’t been done in over three months) and clean out whatever he or she finds within. It’s a highly amusing vignette, and one which Adams has the genius to turn into a major plot point.<br /><br />Having now re-read the whole canon, I think I’m qualified to examine Dirk Gently as a detective – and I find he actually has a great deal in common with Sherlock Holmes. (A man with whom he has fundamental differences on the subject of eliminating the impossible). Like Holmes he seems to be asexual, with a love of clutter and a great deal of esoteric information at his fingertips. Indeed he is possibly even more observant than Sherlock, as there are things that Dirk would spot which Sherlock would never give a moment’s credence to. Unfortunately though, there isn’t a John Watson equivalent on the scene to recount episode after episode of this great man’s adventures, but then Gently may be an even more infuriating person to hang around with than his Baker Street colleague.<br /><br />Indeed this tale opens with Gently’s secretary, having finally abandoned him, working at the check-in at Heathrow Terminal Two. When a passenger can’t board a plane the check-in desk shoots suddenly, and inexplicably, hundreds of feet into the air. From there we encounter angry eagles, mysterious Coke machines, one of the most truly bizarre murders in fiction (which is then, truly bizarrely, labelled a suicide by the police) and the entrance to Valhalla through London’s St Pancras station. Once again Adams’ plotting is not as strong as it could be, and the final quarter does drag somewhat, but it’s brilliantly written and the jokes do keep coming.<br /><br />It is a real shame that Adams died and we don’t have half a dozen more Gently tales (though given his productivity, that probably would have been unlikely anyway). But at least we have the two, and I promise it won’t be another twenty years before I re-read them again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13696850037546573302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_989806383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989806383" />
    <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas"><img alt="Kaethe Douglas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573927565p2/1072582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/989806383?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaethe Douglas" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas">Kaethe Douglas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17032652859278191744">1 Jan 1988<br/>The travails of trying to order a pizza, Valhalla in London, and unexpected encounters with Thor. I loved it.<br/><br/>16 September, 2012<br/>Tash talked me into watching Thor, which I enjoyed enormously. And it reminded me of Adams' Thor, committing an Act of (a) God, when he can't catch a flight to Oslo.   <span id="freeText17032652859278191744" style="display:none">1 Jan 1988<br />The travails of trying to order a pizza, Valhalla in London, and unexpected encounters with Thor. I loved it.<br /><br />16 September, 2012<br />Tash talked me into watching Thor, which I enjoyed enormously. And it reminded me of Adams' Thor, committing an Act of (a) God, when he can't catch a flight to Oslo. More than thirty years later air travel has only become more annoying.It's still fantastically funny, but I'm aware of a sadness to it that I didn't notice on previous readings. The heroine is a widow, the gods are bewildered, homeless and aimless, the yuppies are as annoying as ever. Adams has trouble with plot, so even after reading this at least three times, I'm not exactly clear on what happened at the climax. But with age I seem to have acquired some acceptance: it doesn't bother me that I don't know the details, since the crux is apparent.I wonder what I'll think of it in another thirty years?<br /><br />27 November, 2016<br />I'm kind of astounded at what I remembered and what I didn't (the bath, but not the eagle). This time I'm amazed by all the threads connecting it to newer works and authors I enjoy. I don't suppose I'll ever stop imaging what else he might have done if he'd lived longer.</span>

<div id="review_1340311681" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1340311681" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1275906-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577915392p2/1275906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1340311681?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/1275906-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1275906-chelsea?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1275906-chelsea?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1275906-chelsea?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1340311681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11992220739669271245">AMAZE-BALLS. Douglas Adams's best work, hands down.<br/><br/>So last year I read all of The Hitchhiker's Guide books and loved them, though by the last one you could tell Adams didn't want to write them anymore. I adored Adams's humor and style, so I was excited to read the two Dirk Gently books. The first book suffered for me a little bit because over the first third of the book was very disconnected. But in this one you can see the connections through the various plotlines early on. In some of Adams's o</span>
  <span id="freeText11992220739669271245" style="display:none">AMAZE-BALLS. Douglas Adams's best work, hands down.<br /><br />So last year I read all of The Hitchhiker's Guide books and loved them, though by the last one you could tell Adams didn't want to write them anymore. I adored Adams's humor and style, so I was excited to read the two Dirk Gently books. The first book suffered for me a little bit because over the first third of the book was very disconnected. But in this one you can see the connections through the various plotlines early on. In some of Adams's other books, the plot seems to jump around randomly, and while random-ness does abound here, it's much easier to see its greater purpose, and how everything fits together, which is why I found the story itself more engaging.<br /><br />And then Adams brought in one of my favorite tropes- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[bringing fictional characters to life. Fictional characters from my favorite brand of mythology, Norse. And Thor was just SO Thor. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I knew at that point I was going to love this.<br /><br />Maybe the mystery itself wasn't as well built as the mystery in the last one, but honestly, I enjoyed the ride a hell of a lot more, the mystery didn't even matter that much. The characters were well-developed, and I liked Kate way more than any of Adams's other female characters. Dirk is still a jerk, of course, but a lot more sympathetic than in the last book, and I loved seeing his methods and the way he approached things.<br /><br />Honestly the only complaint is that the ending is a bit rushed. In fact I went back a few pages to make sure I hadn't missed anything. Having heard things about how Adams approached deadlines, it makes me wonder if maybe he ran out of time, so just wrapped everything up quicker than originally planned. That or he felt the book was getting too long (it is longer than any of the Hitchhiker books, though on par with the first Dirk Gently). Or maybe he just wanted it to be like that. We'll never know.<br /><br />Now I'm a million times sadder about him dying so young :( With this book being so original and so fun, I would have loved to see what else he could do, especially since he pretty much told everyone asking for more Hitchhiker's "fuck you" in Mostly Harmless. Douglas Adams's humor and style was such a gift and literature definitely needs more of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11992220739669271245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1793466513" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1793466513" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1793466513?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1793466513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18326352757946689509">Dirk Gently is a "holistic detective" who makes use of "the fundamental interconnectedness of all things" to solve the whole crime, and find the whole person. He bills for <b>everything</b> but claims that he cannot be considered to have ripped anybody off, because none of his clients ever pay him. I can't speak for the first book, since I read out of order, but he certainly doesn't get paid in this one.<br/><br/>I so wanted to give this book five stars. I love Douglas Adams' humor, and his Hitchhiker's series w</span>
  <span id="freeText18326352757946689509" style="display:none">Dirk Gently is a "holistic detective" who makes use of "the fundamental interconnectedness of all things" to solve the whole crime, and find the whole person. He bills for <b>everything</b> but claims that he cannot be considered to have ripped anybody off, because none of his clients ever pay him. I can't speak for the first book, since I read out of order, but he certainly doesn't get paid in this one.<br /><br />I so wanted to give this book five stars. I love Douglas Adams' humor, and his Hitchhiker's series will always be one of my favorites and a go-to. This, however, fell flat after the first half. The set up was pure Adams' British humor. Ridiculousness for ridiculousness' sake, but then when we get to a point where things must be explained it just falls apart.<br /><br />It seems the Dirk books are about seemingly unconnected narrative threads eventually meeting up and becoming connected, but that didn't happen here. There is an ending of sorts. This was about Thor and Odin, Norse Gods, who have been misplaced and have lost, not only their powers, but also their marbles! Adams attempt to pull the threads together simply caused more confusion for me and the novel felt very unfinished. <br /><br />I think there are parts of this book that could be read alone as an example of Adams' genius, but the novel, taken as a whole, was not successful. I will still read the first because I am a bit of a completest and it was a mistake on my part to read out of order, but I won't be expecting much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18326352757946689509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170442284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170442284" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3125102-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269806247p2/3125102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170442284?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/3125102-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3125102-nathan?shelf=real-world-fantasy">real-world-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3125102-nathan?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170442284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13800267733158847010">The back jacked of this book promised me it was "Funnier than Psycho" and "Shorter than War and Peace." Now, I thought that these were jokes. I assumed that that tag was cute and that it would be quite funny. In fact, funnier than Psycho is about as good as the humor was. It was there, but rarely very funny and generally simply kinda cute. It was in fact shorter than War and Peace. <br/><br/>I didn't expect much for plot. It is a Douglas Adams book after all, but I had hoped for decent characters. Unfortu</span>
  <span id="freeText13800267733158847010" style="display:none">The back jacked of this book promised me it was "Funnier than Psycho" and "Shorter than War and Peace." Now, I thought that these were jokes. I assumed that that tag was cute and that it would be quite funny. In fact, funnier than Psycho is about as good as the humor was. It was there, but rarely very funny and generally simply kinda cute. It was in fact shorter than War and Peace. <br /><br />I didn't expect much for plot. It is a Douglas Adams book after all, but I had hoped for decent characters. Unfortunately there is so much going on that none of the characters has a real chance to develop. The shifting character perspective didn't help either. The book was quite short, and chapters told from multiple character points of view don't really have enough room to let the characters grow, just paint the bare bones plot. <br /><br />The ending was just bad. Not that what happened was bad, but it seemed that Adams' editors told him he needed to cut 50 pages, and he subsequently decided to cut 50 of the last 55. The action was jammed together, not fleshed out, and a little hard to follow. For as mediocre as the rest of the book was, the ending was a let down. <br /><br />I don't think I'd recommend the book to anyone except the most devoted Adams fan. Unless your reading goal includes being able to say "Yeah, I've read ALL of his books," I don't see any reason why you should pick this up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13800267733158847010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=humour">humour</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142953399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9500266331562218111">I'm not sure whether this is the effect of not being jammed into half a train seat by someone twice the size of me, but The Long Dark Tea-time of the Soul seemed less funny but more absorbing than the first book. It helped that it included Norse gods, I think. I had no idea that Douglas Adams had tangled with them.<br/><br/>On the other hand, I don't really think that as much seemed to happen, somehow. Less plates seemed to be spinning. I think that was a good thing for the narrative, but it seemed to mak</span>
  <span id="freeText9500266331562218111" style="display:none">I'm not sure whether this is the effect of not being jammed into half a train seat by someone twice the size of me, but The Long Dark Tea-time of the Soul seemed less funny but more absorbing than the first book. It helped that it included Norse gods, I think. I had no idea that Douglas Adams had tangled with them.<br /><br />On the other hand, I don't really think that as much seemed to happen, somehow. Less plates seemed to be spinning. I think that was a good thing for the narrative, but it seemed to make the second book different in tone from the first... (And then I wonder if that was just because at no point did I have to stuff my Kindle back into a bag and run to get off a train because I was about to miss getting off at the correct station. I suspect I'm more influenced by the circumstances in which I read books than I realise.)<br /><br />So... on some levels, I enjoyed this more than the first book, and on some levels, less. Quite an odd feeling.<br /><br />I do like the nine tenths of the subconscious being given over to penguins.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14134764117448436838">How do you describe Adams' Dirk Gently books? I have a hard time not because they can't be genre-classified but because they don't fit any novel form out there. Stream-of-consciousness on the part of the author? Is Gently the main character? Who is the main character? What is going on? There's one thing going on, though--Adams does a lot of describing. It's a wealth of description. Plot? Pish-tosh! We don't need no stinking plot! That's not why you read an Adams novel anyway. So just let Adams m</span>
  <span id="freeText14134764117448436838" style="display:none">How do you describe Adams' Dirk Gently books? I have a hard time not because they can't be genre-classified but because they don't fit any novel form out there. Stream-of-consciousness on the part of the author? Is Gently the main character? Who is the main character? What is going on? There's one thing going on, though--Adams does a lot of describing. It's a wealth of description. Plot? Pish-tosh! We don't need no stinking plot! That's not why you read an Adams novel anyway. So just let Adams mess with your mind. But if you aren't acquainted with his work, read the first two novels in the Hitchhiker's Guide series first, then come in for a landing on the first Dirk Gently novel. You'll thank me.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140361753" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2140361753?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2140361753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3385599619705015067">I didn’t enjoy this nearly as much as <i>Dirk Gently’s Holistic Detective Agency</i>. It started off interesting, but for some reason I became progressively less interested as the story continued and I put the book down more and more frequently. I also didn’t find it as funny. It had humor, but it didn’t make me laugh as much. I think it intentionally took a more serious tone, which I might have appreciated better if I’d been more interested in the story.<br/> <br/>The first book had a mixture of elements from b</span>
  <span id="freeText3385599619705015067" style="display:none">I didn’t enjoy this nearly as much as <i>Dirk Gently’s Holistic Detective Agency</i>. It started off interesting, but for some reason I became progressively less interested as the story continued and I put the book down more and more frequently. I also didn’t find it as funny. It had humor, but it didn’t make me laugh as much. I think it intentionally took a more serious tone, which I might have appreciated better if I’d been more interested in the story.<br /> <br />The first book had a mixture of elements from both science fiction and fantasy, but I thought it leaned more toward science fiction. This book, on the other hand, was purely in the fantasy category with Norse gods playing a large role in the story. In many ways this reminded me of <i>American Gods</i>, at least in terms of the basic premise, except without the “American” part. This book was published first, so maybe I would feel differently if I had read it first, but I preferred <i>American Gods</i>.<br /><br />I’m not really sure why this one didn’t work as well for me as <i>Dirk Gently</i> did but, by the end, I was happy to be done with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3385599619705015067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
